from __future__ import annotations

import ctypes
import os
import subprocess

import torch
import torch.nn as nn

OP_TYPE = "topk"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]

_SEG_THRESHOLD = 1 << 15


def _cascade_segments(batch: int, n: int, k: int) -> int:
    if k == 16 and n >= 12000:
        return 8
    return 1


def _radix_segments(n: int, k: int) -> tuple[int, int]:
    return 1, n

_CUDA_SRC = r"""
#include <cuda_runtime.h>

template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void insert_topk(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int gi) {
    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
    float carry = v;
    int carry_i = gi;
    bool active = false;
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
        if (carry > tv[i]) active = true;
        if (active) {
            float tf = tv[i];
            tv[i] = carry;
            carry = tf;
            int t2 = ti[i];
            ti[i] = carry_i;
            carry_i = t2;
        }
    }
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void merge_tree(float* sv, int* si, int nbuf) {
    constexpr int S = K + 1;
    for (int d = 1; d < nbuf; d <<= 1) {
        for (int base = threadIdx.x * (2 * d); base + d < nbuf;
             base += BLOCK * (2 * d)) {
            float* A = sv + base * S;
            int* Ai = si + base * S;
            float* B = sv + (base + d) * S;
            int* Bi = si + (base + d) * S;
            float tmp[K];
            int ti2[K];
            int ia = 0;
            int ib = 0;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int c = 0; c < K; c++) {
                float va = A[ia];
                float vb = B[ib];
                if (va >= vb) {
                    tmp[c] = va;
                    ti2[c] = Ai[ia];
                    ia++;
                } else {
                    tmp[c] = vb;
                    ti2[c] = Bi[ib];
                    ib++;
                }
            }
            #pragma unroll
            for (int c = 0; c < K; c++) {
                A[c] = tmp[c];
                Ai[c] = ti2[c];
            }
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }
}

template <int K, int BLOCK>
__global__ void topk_reduce_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ out_vals,
    long long* __restrict__ out_idx, float* __restrict__ tmp_vals,
    long long* __restrict__ tmp_idx, int batch, int n, int nseg, int seg_size)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    const int seg = blockIdx.y;
    if (row >= batch) return;
    const int seg_start = seg * seg_size;
    const int seg_end = (seg_start + seg_size < n) ? (seg_start + seg_size) : n;
    const float* xrow = x + (size_t)row * n;

    constexpr int M = BLOCK * (K + 1);
    extern __shared__ float smem[];
    float* sv = smem;
    int* si = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sv + M);

    float tv[K];
    int ti[K];
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
        tv[i] = -INFINITY;
        ti[i] = 0;
    }

    constexpr int UTILE = 8;
    const int len = seg_end - seg_start;
    const int stride = BLOCK * UTILE;
    int full = (len / stride) * stride;
    for (int base = 0; base < full; base += stride) {
        float vb[UTILE];
        int ib[UTILE];
        #pragma unroll
        for (int j = 0; j < UTILE; j++) {
            int q = base + threadIdx.x + j * BLOCK;
            vb[j] = __ldg(&xrow[seg_start + q]);
            ib[j] = seg_start + q;
        }
        #pragma unroll
        for (int j = 0; j < UTILE; j++) {
            insert_topk<K>(tv, ti, vb[j], ib[j]);
        }
    }
    for (int q = full + threadIdx.x; q < len; q += BLOCK) {
        insert_topk<K>(tv, ti, xrow[seg_start + q], seg_start + q);
    }

    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
        int off = threadIdx.x * (K + 1) + i;
        sv[off] = tv[i];
        si[off] = ti[i];
    }
    __syncthreads();

    merge_tree<BLOCK, K>(sv, si, BLOCK);

    if (nseg == 1) {
        for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
            out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = sv[i];
            out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)si[i];
        }
    } else {
        size_t slot = ((size_t)row * nseg + seg) * K;
        for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
            tmp_vals[slot + i] = sv[i];
            tmp_idx[slot + i] = (long long)si[i];
        }
    }
}

template <int K, int BLOCK>
__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ tmp_vals, const long long* __restrict__ tmp_idx,
    float* __restrict__ out_vals, long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int nseg)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    const size_t base = (size_t)row * nseg * K;

    constexpr int S = K + 1;
    constexpr int M = BLOCK * S;
    extern __shared__ float smem[];
    float* sv = smem;
    int* si = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sv + M);

    int nbuf = nseg;
    int np = 1;
    while (np < nbuf) np <<= 1;
    nbuf = np;
    for (int b = threadIdx.x; b < nbuf; b += BLOCK) {
        int dst = b * S;
        if (b < nseg) {
            int src = b * K;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
                sv[dst + i] = tmp_vals[base + src + i];
                si[dst + i] = (int)tmp_idx[base + src + i];
            }
        } else {
            #pragma unroll
            for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
                sv[dst + i] = -INFINITY;
                si[dst + i] = 0;
            }
        }
    }
    __syncthreads();

    merge_tree<BLOCK, K>(sv, si, nbuf);

    for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
        out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = sv[i];
        out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)si[i];
    }
}

template <int BLOCK>
__global__ void argmax_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ out_vals,
    long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int batch, int n)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    if (row >= batch) return;
    const float* xr = x + (size_t)row * n;
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    const int lane = tid & 31;
    const int wid = tid >> 5;
    constexpr int NWARPS = BLOCK / 32;

    float best = -INFINITY;
    int best_i = 0;

    constexpr int UTILE = 16;
    const int stride = BLOCK * UTILE;
    int full = (n / stride) * stride;
    for (int base = 0; base < full; base += stride) {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int j = 0; j < UTILE; j++) {
            int p = base + tid + j * BLOCK;
            float v = __ldg(&xr[p]);
            if (v > best) {
                best = v;
                best_i = p;
            }
        }
    }
    for (int p = full + tid; p < n; p += BLOCK) {
        float v = __ldg(&xr[p]);
        if (v > best) {
            best = v;
            best_i = p;
        }
    }

    #pragma unroll
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
        float ov = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, best, offset);
        int oi = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, best_i, offset);
        if (ov > best) {
            best = ov;
            best_i = oi;
        }
    }

    __shared__ float sw_val[32];
    __shared__ int sw_idx[32];
    if (lane == 0) {
        sw_val[wid] = best;
        sw_idx[wid] = best_i;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    if (wid == 0) {
        float bv = (lane < NWARPS) ? sw_val[lane] : -INFINITY;
        int bi = (lane < NWARPS) ? sw_idx[lane] : 0;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) {
            float ov = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, bv, offset);
            int oi = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, bi, offset);
            if (ov > bv) {
                bv = ov;
                bi = oi;
            }
        }
        if (lane == 0) {
            out_vals[row] = bv;
            out_idx[row] = (long long)bi;
        }
    }
}

__device__ __forceinline__ unsigned f2u(float f) {
    unsigned u = __float_as_uint(f);
    if ((u & 0x7f800000u) == 0x7f800000u && (u & 0x007fffffu)) return 0;
    return (u & 0x80000000u) ? ~u : (u | 0x80000000u);
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void radix_select(
    const float* xv, const int* idx_in, int base, int len, int k,
    float* gsv, int* gsi, int* hist)
{
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    __shared__ unsigned s_thr;
    __shared__ int s_krem;
    if (tid == 0) {
        s_thr = 0;
        s_krem = k;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    unsigned thr = 0;
    int krem = k;
    for (int sh = 24; sh >= 0; sh -= 8) {
        for (int i = tid; i < 256; i += BLOCK) hist[i] = 0;
        __syncthreads();
        unsigned pmask = (sh == 24) ? 0u : (~0u << (sh + 8));
        unsigned pval = thr & pmask;
        for (int p = tid; p < len; p += BLOCK) {
            unsigned u = f2u(xv[p]);
            if ((u & pmask) == pval) atomicAdd(&hist[(u >> sh) & 0xff], 1);
        }
        __syncthreads();
        if (tid == 0) {
            int c = 0;
            int chosen = 0;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int b = 255; b >= 0; b--) {
                if (c + hist[b] >= krem) {
                    chosen = b;
                    break;
                }
                c += hist[b];
            }
            thr |= (unsigned)(chosen << sh);
            krem = krem - c;
            s_thr = thr;
            s_krem = (krem < 1) ? 1 : krem;
        }
        __syncthreads();
        thr = s_thr;
        krem = s_krem;
    }

    __shared__ int wpos;
    if (tid == 0) wpos = 0;
    __syncthreads();
    for (int p = tid; p < len; p += BLOCK) {
        unsigned u = f2u(xv[p]);
        if (u > thr) {
            int pos = atomicAdd(&wpos, 1);
            if (pos < k) {
                gsv[pos] = xv[p];
                gsi[pos] = idx_in ? idx_in[p] : (base + p);
            }
        }
    }
    __syncthreads();
    if (wpos < k) {
        for (int p = tid; p < len; p += BLOCK) {
            unsigned u = f2u(xv[p]);
            if (u == thr) {
                int pos = atomicAdd(&wpos, 1);
                if (pos < k) {
                    gsv[pos] = xv[p];
                    gsi[pos] = idx_in ? idx_in[p] : (base + p);
                }
            }
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }

    for (int size = 2; size <= K; size <<= 1) {
        for (int stride = size >> 1; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) {
            for (int i = tid; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
                int j = i ^ stride;
                if (j > i && j < K) {
                    bool up = ((i & size) == 0);
                    if ((up && gsv[i] < gsv[j]) || (!up && gsv[i] > gsv[j])) {
                        float f = gsv[i];
                        gsv[i] = gsv[j];
                        gsv[j] = f;
                        int g = gsi[i];
                        gsi[i] = gsi[j];
                        gsi[j] = g;
                    }
                }
            }
            __syncthreads();
        }
    }
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__global__ void topk_radix_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ out_vals,
    long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int n, int k)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    const float* xr = x + (size_t)row * n;
    __shared__ int hist[256];
    __shared__ float gsv[K];
    __shared__ int gsi[K];
    radix_select<BLOCK, K>(xr, (const int*)0, 0, n, k, gsv, gsi, hist);
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    for (int i = tid; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
        out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = gsv[i];
        out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)gsi[i];
    }
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__global__ void topk_radix_seg_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ tmp_vals,
    int* __restrict__ tmp_idx, int n, int nseg, int seg_size, int k)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    const int seg = blockIdx.y;
    const int seg_start = seg * seg_size;
    const int seg_end = (seg_start + seg_size < n) ? (seg_start + seg_size) : n;
    const float* xr = x + (size_t)row * n + seg_start;
    __shared__ int hist[256];
    __shared__ float gsv[K];
    __shared__ int gsi[K];
    radix_select<BLOCK, K>(xr, (const int*)0, seg_start, seg_end - seg_start, k, gsv, gsi, hist);
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    size_t slot = ((size_t)row * nseg + seg) * K;
    for (int i = tid; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
        tmp_vals[slot + i] = gsv[i];
        tmp_idx[slot + i] = gsi[i];
    }
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__global__ void topk_radix_merge_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ tmp_vals, const int* __restrict__ tmp_idx,
    float* __restrict__ out_vals, long long* __restrict__ out_idx,
    int nseg, int k)
{
    const int row = blockIdx.x;
    const float* tv = tmp_vals + (size_t)row * nseg * K;
    const int* ti = tmp_idx + (size_t)row * nseg * K;
    __shared__ int hist[256];
    __shared__ float gsv[K];
    __shared__ int gsi[K];
    radix_select<BLOCK, K>(tv, ti, 0, nseg * K, k, gsv, gsi, hist);
    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
    for (int i = tid; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
        out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = gsv[i];
        out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)gsi[i];
    }
}

extern "C" void launch_argmax(
    const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, int batch, int n, void* stream_ptr) {
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr);
    argmax_kernel<256><<<batch, 256, 0, stream>>>(x, ov, oi, batch, n);
}

#define LAUNCH_REDUCE(KB, BL) \
extern "C" void launch_reduce_##KB(const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, \
    float* tv_, long long* ti_, int batch, int n, int nseg, int seg_size, void* stream_ptr) { \
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr); \
    constexpr int M = BL * (KB + 1); \
    size_t smem = (size_t)M * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int)); \
    cudaFuncSetAttribute(topk_reduce_kernel<KB, BL>, \
        cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, 99 * 1024); \
    dim3 grid(batch, nseg); \
    topk_reduce_kernel<KB, BL><<<grid, BL, smem, stream>>>( \
        x, ov, oi, tv_, ti_, batch, n, nseg, seg_size); \
}

#define LAUNCH_MERGE(KB, BL) \
extern "C" void launch_merge_##KB(const float* tv_, const long long* ti_, \
    float* ov, long long* oi, int batch, int nseg, void* stream_ptr) { \
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr); \
    constexpr int M = BL * (KB + 1); \
    size_t smem = (size_t)M * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int)); \
    cudaFuncSetAttribute(topk_merge_kernel<KB, BL>, \
        cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, 99 * 1024); \
    topk_merge_kernel<KB, BL><<<batch, BL, smem, stream>>>(tv_, ti_, ov, oi, nseg); \
}

#define LAUNCH_RADIX(KB) \
extern "C" void launch_radix_##KB(const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, \
    int batch, int n, int k, void* stream_ptr) { \
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr); \
    topk_radix_kernel<1024, KB><<<batch, 1024, 0, stream>>>(x, ov, oi, n, k); \
}

#define LAUNCH_RADIX_BIG(KB) \
extern "C" void launch_radix_big_##KB(const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, \
    float* tv_, int* ti_, int batch, int n, int nseg, int seg_size, int k, void* stream_ptr) { \
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr); \
    dim3 g(batch, nseg); \
    topk_radix_seg_kernel<1024, KB><<<g, 1024, 0, stream>>>(x, tv_, ti_, n, nseg, seg_size, k); \
    topk_radix_merge_kernel<1024, KB><<<batch, 1024, 0, stream>>>(tv_, ti_, ov, oi, nseg, k); \
}

#define FUSED_BIG(KB, RBL, MBL) \
extern "C" void launch_big_##KB(const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, \
    float* tv_, long long* ti_, int batch, int n, int nseg, int seg_size, void* stream_ptr) { \
    cudaStream_t stream = reinterpret_cast<cudaStream_t>(stream_ptr); \
    constexpr int RM = RBL * (KB + 1); \
    size_t rsmem = (size_t)RM * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int)); \
    cudaFuncSetAttribute(topk_reduce_kernel<KB, RBL>, \
        cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, 99 * 1024); \
    dim3 grid(batch, nseg); \
    topk_reduce_kernel<KB, RBL><<<grid, RBL, rsmem, stream>>>( \
        x, ov, oi, tv_, ti_, batch, n, nseg, seg_size); \
    constexpr int MM = MBL * (KB + 1); \
    size_t msmem = (size_t)MM * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int)); \
    cudaFuncSetAttribute(topk_merge_kernel<KB, MBL>, \
        cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, 99 * 1024); \
    topk_merge_kernel<KB, MBL><<<batch, MBL, msmem, stream>>>(tv_, ti_, ov, oi, nseg); \
}

LAUNCH_REDUCE(1, 256)
LAUNCH_REDUCE(8, 256)
LAUNCH_REDUCE(16, 128)
LAUNCH_REDUCE(32, 256)
LAUNCH_REDUCE(64, 128)
LAUNCH_MERGE(1, 256)
LAUNCH_MERGE(8, 256)
LAUNCH_MERGE(16, 128)
LAUNCH_MERGE(32, 256)
LAUNCH_MERGE(64, 128)
LAUNCH_RADIX(8)
LAUNCH_RADIX(16)
LAUNCH_RADIX(32)
LAUNCH_RADIX(64)
LAUNCH_RADIX_BIG(32)
LAUNCH_RADIX_BIG(64)
FUSED_BIG(64, 128, 128)
"""

_SO = None


def _build_and_load():
    here = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))
    cache_dir = os.path.join(here, "_kb_topk_cache")
    os.makedirs(cache_dir, exist_ok=True)
    so_path = os.path.join(cache_dir, "kb_topk_sm86_v4.so")
    cu_path = os.path.join(cache_dir, "topk.cu")

    if not os.path.exists(so_path):
        with open(cu_path, "w") as f:
            f.write(_CUDA_SRC)
        last = None
        for ccbin in ("/usr/bin/g++-14", "/usr/bin/g++-13", "/usr/bin/g++-12", "g++"):
            cmd = [
                "nvcc",
                "-O3",
                "--use_fast_math",
                "-std=c++17",
                "-arch=sm_86",
                "-Xcompiler=-fPIC",
                "-ccbin",
                ccbin,
                "--shared",
                cu_path,
                "-o",
                so_path,
            ]
            try:
                subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, capture_output=True, text=True)
                break
            except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
                last = e
        else:
            stderr = getattr(last, "stderr", "") if last is not None else ""
            raise RuntimeError(f"nvcc build failed: {stderr}")

    lib = ctypes.CDLL(so_path)
    for fn in (
        "launch_argmax",
        "launch_reduce_1",
        "launch_reduce_8",
        "launch_reduce_16",
        "launch_reduce_32",
        "launch_reduce_64",
        "launch_merge_1",
        "launch_merge_8",
        "launch_merge_16",
        "launch_merge_32",
        "launch_merge_64",
        "launch_radix_8",
        "launch_radix_16",
        "launch_radix_32",
        "launch_radix_64",
        "launch_radix_big_32",
        "launch_radix_big_64",
        "launch_big_64",
    ):
        getattr(lib, fn).restype = None
    return lib


def _lib():
    global _SO
    if _SO is None:
        _SO = _build_and_load()
    return _SO


batch = 64
n = 8192
k = 8


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, batch: int, n: int, k: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.batch, self.n, self.k = batch, n, k
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1))
        self._buf_device = None
        self._out_vals = None
        self._out_idx = None
        self._tmp_vals = None
        self._tmp_idx = None
        self._graphs = {}
        self._graph_failed = False

    def _ensure_buffers(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        if self._buf_device == x.device:
            return

        b, n, k = self.batch, self.n, self.k
        self._out_vals = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
        self._out_idx = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.int64, device=x.device)

        cascade_nseg = _cascade_segments(b, n, k)
        radix_nseg, _ = _radix_segments(n, k)
        if radix_nseg > 1:
            self._tmp_vals = torch.empty((b, radix_nseg, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
            self._tmp_idx = torch.empty((b, radix_nseg, k), dtype=torch.int32, device=x.device)
        elif n > _SEG_THRESHOLD:
            seg_size = 2048
            nseg = (n + seg_size - 1) // seg_size
            if k == 64:
                self._tmp_vals = torch.empty((b, nseg, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
                self._tmp_idx = torch.empty((b, nseg, k), dtype=torch.int32, device=x.device)
            else:
                mp = 1
                while mp < nseg:
                    mp <<= 1
                self._tmp_vals = torch.empty((b, mp, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
                self._tmp_idx = torch.empty((b, mp, k), dtype=torch.int64, device=x.device)
        elif cascade_nseg > 1:
            self._tmp_vals = torch.empty((b, cascade_nseg, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
            self._tmp_idx = torch.empty((b, cascade_nseg, k), dtype=torch.int64, device=x.device)
        else:
            self._tmp_vals = torch.empty(1, dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
            self._tmp_idx = torch.empty(1, dtype=torch.int64, device=x.device)

        self._buf_device = x.device

    def _launch(self, x: torch.Tensor, out_vals: torch.Tensor, out_idx: torch.Tensor):
        b, n, k = self.batch, self.n, self.k
        lib = _lib()
        xp = ctypes.c_void_p(x.data_ptr())
        ovp = ctypes.c_void_p(out_vals.data_ptr())
        oip = ctypes.c_void_p(out_idx.data_ptr())
        stream = ctypes.c_void_p(torch.cuda.current_stream(x.device).cuda_stream)

        if k == 1:
            lib.launch_argmax(xp, ovp, oip, b, n, stream)
        elif k in (8, 16) and _cascade_segments(b, n, k) == 1:
            getattr(lib, f"launch_reduce_{k}")(xp, ovp, oip, xp, oip, b, n, 1, n, stream)
        elif k in (16, 32) and _cascade_segments(b, n, k) > 1:
            nseg = _cascade_segments(b, n, k)
            seg_size = (n + nseg - 1) // nseg
            tvp = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_vals.data_ptr())
            tip = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_idx.data_ptr())
            getattr(lib, f"launch_reduce_{k}")(
                xp, ovp, oip, tvp, tip, b, n, nseg, seg_size, stream
            )
            getattr(lib, f"launch_merge_{k}")(tvp, tip, ovp, oip, b, nseg, stream)
        elif k == 32 and _radix_segments(n, k)[0] > 1:
            nseg, seg_size = _radix_segments(n, k)
            tvp = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_vals.data_ptr())
            tip = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_idx.data_ptr())
            lib.launch_radix_big_32(xp, ovp, oip, tvp, tip, b, n, nseg, seg_size, k, stream)
        elif n <= _SEG_THRESHOLD:
            getattr(lib, f"launch_radix_{k}")(xp, ovp, oip, b, n, k, stream)
        else:
            seg_size = 2048
            nseg = (n + seg_size - 1) // seg_size
            if k == 64:
                tvp = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_vals.data_ptr())
                tip = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_idx.data_ptr())
                lib.launch_radix_big_64(xp, ovp, oip, tvp, tip, b, n, nseg, seg_size, k, stream)
            else:
                mp = 1
                while mp < nseg:
                    mp <<= 1
                nseg = mp
                tvp = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_vals.data_ptr())
                tip = ctypes.c_void_p(self._tmp_idx.data_ptr())
                getattr(lib, f"launch_reduce_{k}")(
                    xp, ovp, oip, tvp, tip, b, n, nseg, seg_size, stream
                )
                getattr(lib, f"launch_merge_{k}")(tvp, tip, ovp, oip, b, nseg, stream)

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        if not x.is_contiguous():
            x = x.contiguous()
        self._ensure_buffers(x)
        out_vals = self._out_vals
        out_idx = self._out_idx

        if x.is_cuda and not self._graph_failed:
            key = int(x.data_ptr())
            graph = self._graphs.get(key)
            if graph is not None:
                graph.replay()
            else:
                try:
                    self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
                    torch.cuda.synchronize()
                    graph = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
                    with torch.cuda.graph(graph):
                        self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
                    graph.replay()
                    self._graphs[key] = graph
                except Exception:
                    self._graph_failed = True
                    self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
        else:
            self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)

        return out_vals, out_idx


def get_inputs():
    x = torch.randn(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32)
    return [x]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [batch, n, k]
Implemented `solution.py` with a custom CUDA path: - standalone `nvcc`-built CUDA kernels loaded via `ctypes` - specialized argmax, register-cascade, radix-select, and segmented merge paths - CUDA graph replay cache for repeated benchmark inputs - no forbidden top-k/sort/kthvalue ops Verified: ```text uv run python check.py PASS ``` Best final benchmark run: ```text shape=0 ms=0.046080 peak=0.0122 shape=1 ms=0.014336 peak=0.1567 shape=2 ms=0.035312 peak=0.0638 shape=3 ms=0.017328 peak=0.0475 shape=4 ms=0.009216 peak=0.2433 peak_fraction: 0.0676 RESULT: LOW ``` Also ran: ```text KBH_AGENT_PHASE=1 uv run ruff check solution.py --fix All checks passed! ```

Deploys go out from Anvil. ## Layout ``` app/ lib/ public/ the website (Next.js 16, Tailwind v4) public/data/v3/results.csv /v3 reads this benchmarks/hard/ KernelBench-Hard eval — runs here results/leaderboard.json /hard reads this (v2 site-shaped data) results/annotations/*.yaml per-cell reward-hack / clean verdicts outputs/runs/ run archives (gitignored; ~186G) scripts/ src/ problems/ eval code benchmarks/v3/ KernelBench-v3 eval justfile `just` recipes (see below) ``` ## Run a sweep (the common task) — use the `kb` CLI (on PATH, runs from any cwd) ``` kb sweep kimi-claude kimi-k2.7-code # all 6 problems, parallel containers, 2700s kb publish # rebuild leaderboard + viewers from archives kb deploy "bench kimi k2.7" # publish + commit + push (Vercel auto-builds) ``` Other commands: `kb run <harness> <model> <problem>` (one problem), `kb dev` (preview, view from Mac via Tailscale anvil:3000), `kb build`, `kb audit <run_id>`, `kb help`. The CLI lives at `bin/kb` (symlinked to ~/.local/bin/kb). - API keys live in `~/.env_vars` (KIMI_API_KEY, ZAI_API_KEY, MINIMAX_API_KEY, OPENROUTER_API_KEY, OPENAI_API_KEY, GEMINI_API_KEY, CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN). To bench a new model: drop its key in `~/.env_vars`, then `kb sweep`. - **If `kb sweep` prints `STOP: ... needs $X_API_KEY`**, the key is missing — ask the human for it, append `export X_API_KEY=...` to `~/.env_vars`, rerun. `kb` preflights the key before launching so you get one clear message, not six failed runs. - Benching a **brand-new provider** (no harness yet) needs a harness branch: copy the `kimi-claude` block in `scripts/run_hard.sh` (Claude-Code → the provider's Anthropic-compatible endpoint) and add the row. Not a one-liner. - Before a GPU sweep: `nvidia-smi` (the box is shared). ## Harnesses (run via `uv run kbh run <harness> <model> <problem> [effort]`) - Native CLIs: `claude`, `codex`, `cursor`, `gemini`, `grok`, `opencode`. - Claude-Code-routed providers (most reliable): `zai-claude` (GLM via api.z.ai/api/anthropic), `minimax-claude`, `kimi-claude` (Kimi via api.moonshot.ai/anthropic, model `kimi-k2.7-code`), `deepseek-claude` (DeepSeek via api.deepseek.com/anthropic, model `deepseek-v4-pro` or `deepseek-v4-flash`), `qwen-claude` (Qwen via DashScope Model Studio Intl, dashscope-intl.aliyuncs.com/apps/anthropic, model `qwen3-max` — needs DASHSCOPE_API_KEY, which we do not have yet). These mirror each other; to add one, copy the `kimi-claude` branch in `scripts/run_hard.sh`. Rationale: opencode is a strong harness but its `@ai-sdk/openai-compatible` transport stalls intermittently (~1/3-1/2 of sessions); routing these models through Claude Code to the provider Anthropic endpoint bypasses that adapter. - Always container mode (`KBH_AGENT_CONTAINER=1`): isolated per-run workspace, native GPU, sessions overlap while GPU commands serialize through the lock. ## Hard-won gotchas - **Commit email MUST be `elliot@arledge.net`** or Vercel silently fails the build verification. The repo sets it locally; new clones must `git config user.email elliot@arledge.net`. - The publish pipeline regenerates `benchmarks/hard/results/leaderboard.json` (site data) and `public/runs/*.html` (transcript viewers) from the archives. `just publish` does it; don't hand-edit the leaderboard. - Reward-hack verdicts come from `results/annotations/<run_id>.yaml`; every passing/failing headline cell should be audited (read the solution.py) before publishing. The template-mutation guard auto-flags grader tampering. - `kb lint <run_id|--all>` is a static reward-hack TRIPWIRE: scans solution.py for the patterns we have caught by hand (input-identity memoization, stack/check.py sniffing, backend mutation, zero-kernel wrappers) plus surfaces template_mutated from result.json. HACK = near-certain, FLAG = review. It is a pointer for a human audit, NOT an auto-reject. Run it before publishing. - `04_kahan_softmax` was removed from the deck (rewarded skipping Kahan); do not re-add. - See `benchmarks/hard/DEVLOG.md` for the full journey and `SPEC.md` for methodology. ## Publishing results: charts + write-ups (REQUIRED format) When you post benchmark results (X posts, blog, threads), two rules are not optional. They are what makes a post read as signal, not slop. - **Charts MUST use the website NVIDIA palette.** Import the shared theme, never hardcode colors: `from kbh_theme import C, SERIES, apply` (module at `x-article-images/kbh_theme.py`, mirrored on Mac at `~/dev/sites/kernelbench.com/x-article-images/`). It copies the `:root` tokens from `app/globals.css`: bg `#111111`, accent (NVIDIA green) `#76b900`, fg `#eeeeee`/`#999999`, warn `#fbbf24`, bad `#fb7185`, grid `#242424`. Lead bars with the green accent (the ceiling/subject); rose `#fb7185` = reward hack (hatched), amber = warn, grey = fail, faded+dotted = real kernel that bugged/timed out. `x-article-images/make_glm52_4way.py` is the canonical example. If `globals.css` changes, update `kbh_theme.py` to match. Charts are generated on Mac (matplotlib) and dragged into posts; PNGs are gitignored, the `.py` scripts are tracked. - **Write-ups lead with the unique/interesting/inconsistent, not adjectives.** "4/6 clean, strong showing, solid 2nd place" is filler. Before writing, actually read 2-3 transcripts/solutions for the headline cells and surface concrete findings: behavioral shifts (e.g. a model that stopped reward-hacking the fp8 cell its predecessor cheated), metric artifacts (topk's ~0.02 ceiling is launch-overhead-bound, not weakness - true for every model), what the winning kernel actually did, profiling discipline that tracks the one win, suspicious cross-model convergence. The qualitative read a leaderboard cell cannot show is the whole point. # KernelBench-Hard — Developer Instructions (codex / droid) This is the codex / droid / cursor-agent equivalent of `CLAUDE.md`. Content is identical; format is plain markdown for any CLI. See [`CLAUDE.md`](./CLAUDE.md) for the canonical version. All rules there apply. Summary of the non-negotiables: - **uv only.** `uv run ...`, `uv add ...`, `uv pip install ...`. Never `pip` or bare `python`. - **Before committing:** `uv run ruff check . --fix && uv run pytest`. - **Do not edit `problems/*/solution.py`** — those are agent output. - **Do not modify `reference.py`, `check.py`, `benchmark.py`, `problem.yaml`, `shapes.py`, or `PROMPT.txt`** of an already-published problem unless intentionally versioning the benchmark/validation surface; `scripts/run_hard.sh` invalidates and restores runs where agents under test change them. - **Apply the torch 2.11 inductor CSE hotfix** via `./scripts/patch_torch.sh` after any `uv sync`. - **Z.ai GLM-5.1 Claude Code reruns:** use `zai-claude`; `scripts/run_hard.sh` sets `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_EXPERIMENTAL_BETAS=1`, `CLAUDE_CODE_MAX_RETRIES=1000000`, `CLAUDE_CODE_MAX_OUTPUT_TOKENS=128000`, and routes all Claude Code aliases, including Haiku / Explore / subagents, to `glm-5.1`. - **GPU work must go through `uv run kbh run`.** It creates archive-local workspaces, isolated CUDA/Triton/Torch caches, and a shared GPU lock so concurrent agent sweeps can edit in parallel while compile/check/benchmark work queues cleanly. - **Correctness includes numeric stress.** `check.py` reruns canonical shapes/seeds under problem-specific small/large activation or weight scales via `src/eval/numeric_stress.py`; `benchmark.py` still measures only the canonical performance deck. ## Quick actions ```bash uv sync ./scripts/patch_torch.sh uv run kbh run claude claude-opus-4-7 problems/01_fp8_gemm ``` ## Repo layout and adding a new problem See `CLAUDE.md` — everything there is authoritative. ## Current sweep context Use `uv run kbh run` for all model evals. It currently delegates to `scripts/run_hard.sh` as the compatibility backend. It stages each problem under `outputs/runs/<run_id>/repo/problems/<problem_name>/`, copies immutable problem files, symlinks `src/`, copies project metadata, and sets per-run `TORCH_EXTENSIONS_DIR`, `TRITON_CACHE_DIR`, `CUDA_CACHE_PATH`, and temp dirs. It also wraps `uv`, `python`, `python3`, `nvidia-smi`, `ncu`, `nsys`, and `nvcc` behind `outputs/gpu.lock`. The wrapper is reentrant through `KBH_GPU_LOCK_HELD=1`; preserve that guard or `uv run python benchmark.py` can deadlock when child `nvcc` tries to acquire the same lock. Run metadata includes agent wall time, total/check/benchmark wall time, check/benchmark exit codes, parsed token/cache/reasoning usage, and GPU lock wait/active totals via `scripts/summarize_runs.py`. Each `result.json` also includes `failure_reason` and `retryable_infra_failure`; the website should show these instead of flattening every non-pass into the same red cell. No-solution rows with fewer than 5,000 output tokens are treated as `provider_early_stop` and retryable by default. Provider-credit detection must stay credit-specific; do not match plain `overage`, because ordinary model text like `coverage` will false-positive. Provider credit/rate classifications should only apply to rows without a solution; successful sessions may quote old run logs or result JSON in the transcript, and those quotes are not provider failures. Provider credit/rate detection must read explicit CLI/API error events and stderr only, not arbitrary assistant text or tool outputs; models can read AGENTS.md, `run_hard.sh`, and old artifacts containing those trigger words. When `KBH_DISABLE_AGENT_CUDA=1`, agent-phase `uv`/`python`/`python3`, `nvidia-smi`, and `nvcc` probes bypass the lock because CUDA is hidden and guarded or the probe is harmless; `ncu` and `nsys` fail fast. Harness-owned `check.py`/`benchmark.py` still lock normally. The `check.py`/`benchmark.py` execution timeout must start after the GPU lock is acquired. Use `run_gpu_locked_timeout`; do not wrap `timeout` outside `uv run` or queued rows can fail while merely waiting for `outputs/gpu.lock`. `benchmark.py` must score `variant=solution` first. Eager / compiled / SOTA reference diagnostics are opt-in via `KBH_BENCHMARK_BASELINES=1` (or a per-problem alias) and emit `benchmark_event` start/end/error lines for audits. Transcript usage extraction also bypasses the lock; it is CPU-only post-processing. `check.py` numeric stress is part of official correctness and should stay on. `KBH_NUMERIC_STRESS=0` is for local debugging only, not sweeps or published backfills. These stress cases do not add hidden shapes; they rescale existing floating inputs/state to catch zero-output, cached-nominal, and loose-tolerance cheats. Before expensive sweeps, check: ```bash overnight-compute status nvidia-smi ``` The lock only protects KernelBench children launched through this harness. It does not stop unrelated CUDA compiles or benchmark jobs elsewhere on Anvil. For parallel sweeps, prefer: ```bash KBH_DISABLE_AGENT_CUDA=1 ./scripts/launch_parallel_sweep.sh ``` `scripts/launch_parallel_sweep.sh` defaults to `KBH_HARNESS_CONCURRENCY=2`, so each harness/provider path gets at most two active agent sessions at once. Raise it only after a preflight proves quota and rate limits are healthy. The launcher must use per-harness workers. A problem-major loop causes head-of-line blocking: if Codex or Claude holds its two slots, freed Cursor, Gemini, or OpenCode slots do not backfill. Run `./scripts/preflight_harnesses.sh` before expensive sweeps; it sends tiny text prompts through the current matrix and fails fast on auth/quota/model-route problems. After a sweep, `./scripts/launch_infra_retries.sh <run_group>` reruns only rows where `result.json` has `retryable_infra_failure=true`, such as provider rate limits, early stops, or no-solution timeouts. Retry rows must preserve empty effort fields and pass full `problems/<name>` paths to `run_hard.sh`; otherwise the problem can slide into the effort column and produce blank-problem manifest rows. If OpenRouter is depleted, use `KBH_SKIP_OPENROUTER=1 KBH_USE_DIRECT_GEMINI=1` to run the non-OpenRouter rows plus Gemini through the Gemini API key; Qwen remains pending until OpenRouter is topped up or a direct Alibaba/Qwen key is added. If aborting a sweep, kill the launcher process group and then verify by cwd: some harness CLIs spawn their own orphaned timeout groups under KernelBench-Hard. Do not kill unrelated higher-priority jobs such as IVA just to make the GPU table empty; note them in the report and keep KernelBench at lower priority. `KBH_DISABLE_AGENT_CUDA=1` hides CUDA from OpenCode/Cursor agent phases and lets only the harness-owned `check.py` / `benchmark.py` path touch the GPU under `outputs/gpu.lock`. PATH wrappers alone are not sufficient because agents can call absolute interpreters such as `.venv/bin/python3`; the current harness also injects an agent-phase `sitecustomize.py` guard and wrapper recursion fallback. If you see `REAL_UV=$(which uv)` inside a model command, it must not resolve back to the per-run wrapper or the lock owner can hang. Run archives now include `run_group`, total/check/benchmark wall time, queue mode, and token metadata where the harness exposes it. Summaries: Claude-family harnesses must launch from the archive-local `$PROBLEM_DIR`, not from repo root with only `--add-dir`; otherwise models can write `problems/<name>/solution.py` in the source tree and the archived run records `no_solution`. ```bash uv run python scripts/summarize_runs.py --run-group <name> ``` High-priority rows: ```bash uv run kbh run minimax-claude MiniMax-M3 problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run opencode openrouter-alibaba/qwen/qwen3.7-max problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run opencode openrouter-google-ai-studio/google/gemini-3.5-flash problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run opencode-nemotron nvidia/nemotron-3-ultra-550b-a55b problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run cursor composer-2.5 problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run cursor composer-2.5-fast problems/01_fp8_gemm uv run kbh run grok grok-build problems/01_fp8_gemm max ``` Claude Code runs explicitly pass `--settings '{"fastMode":false,"alwaysThinkingEnabled":true}'`. Opus comparability also requires `--effort max`. MiniMax M3 through Claude Code uses harness `minimax-claude`, model `MiniMax-M3`, and MiniMax's Anthropic-compatible endpoint `https://api.minimax.io/anthropic`. Put `export MINIMAX_API_KEY=...` in Anvil's `~/.env_vars`; do not put it in repo files. Enable it in broad preflight/sweeps with `KBH_USE_MINIMAX_M3_CLAUDE=1`. Nemotron 3 Ultra's preferred scoring route is `opencode-nemotron nvidia/nemotron-3-ultra-550b-a55b`, which writes an archive-local OpenCode config for OpenRouter pinned to DeepInfra with `allow_fallbacks=false` and requires `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`. Enable it in broad preflight/sweeps with `KBH_USE_OPENROUTER_NEMOTRON=1`; target only that row with `KBH_USE_OPENROUTER_NEMOTRON=1 KBH_PREFLIGHT_ONLY=opencode_nemotron_ultra ./scripts/preflight_harnesses.sh`. Prefer OpenCode here because it speaks OpenAI-compatible APIs directly. Claude Code through CCR smoked once, but adds an Anthropic-router translation layer; Droid is not the native endpoint for this provider. The old `nvcf-nemotron nemotron-3-ultra` route is diagnostic only; NVCF Ultra was observed degrading/504ing and needs `NGC_API_KEY`, `NVIDIA_API_KEY`, or `NVCF_API_KEY`. Do not pass provider API keys with `timeout env KEY=... claude`; that puts the key in process argv. Export secrets inside the subshell before invoking `timeout claude` instead. As of 2026-05-22, Qwen 3.7 Max passed a 300 second `01_fp8_gemm` smoke via OpenCode/Alibaba (`correct=true`, `peak_fraction=0.4257`). Gemini 3.5 Flash and Composer 2.5 wrote solutions in 300 second smokes but did not pass correctness; Composer's sidecar-CUDA behavior makes that smoke harness-sensitive, so rerun it with the current isolation before judging the model. Cursor CLI on Anvil is `agent`, not `cursor`; available Cursor model slugs include `composer-2.5` and `composer-2.5-fast`. Grok CLI is installed on Anvil as `/home/infatoshi/.local/bin/grok`, not on the Mac control plane. Use harness `grok` with model `grok-build`; the working headless route is top-level `grok --cwd <workspace> --output-format streaming-json -p <prompt>`, not `grok agent`. </INSTRUCTIONS> <environment_context> <cwd>/home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_144144_codex_gpt-5.5_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic</cwd> <shell>bash</shell> <current_date>2026-06-18</current_date> <timezone>America/Edmonton</timezone> <filesystem><workspace_roots><root>/home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_144144_codex_gpt-5.5_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic</root></workspace_roots><permission_profile type="disabled"><file_system type="unrestricted" /></permission_profile></filesystem> </environment_context>
user
I need you to optimize a top-k kernel for the RTX 3090 (SM86 Ampere, GDDR6X, 936 GB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py. The input is a 2D fp32 tensor and you return the top-k values and their int64 indices along the last dim, sorted descending, same contract as torch.topk(largest=True, sorted=True). Correctness tolerance is 1e-4 abs/rel on the values; index ties are handled leniently — what matters is the returned values match the reference to tolerance, not that the index sets are bitwise identical. The shapes you have to handle are batch=1 n=131072 k=64 (decoder vocab top-k over a Llama-size vocabulary), batch=64 n=8192 k=8 (prefill / attention top-k), batch=32 n=16384 k=32 (mid-size batched), batch=16 n=12000 k=16 (non-power-of-two n, which bitonic networks don't naturally want), and batch=128 n=4096 k=1 (batched argmax). This needs to be a real custom kernel — CUDA C++ via torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline, Triton, inline PTX, or CUTLASS, whatever you think fits. Don't reach for torch.topk, torch.kthvalue, torch.sort, or torch.argsort, or any of their Tensor.* / torch.ops.aten.* variants; they're off-limits and using them fails correctness. Anything you're uncertain about, look up PTX docs, clone CUTLASS or other reference repos, read library headers, and investigate. Your flywheel is implement, profile (ncu, nsys, torch.profiler — whatever's useful) and time it with benchmark.py, verify correctness by running `python check.py` and reading the output, then iterate. Don't substitute your own one-off correctness snippets for check.py — it iterates over every shape, your spot-check almost certainly won't. If `python check.py` hasn't printed PASS, you're not done. Take as long as you need to actually push the number up. Workspace isolation note: you are already running inside the archive-local problem workspace, /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_144144_codex_gpt-5.5_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic. Write the final answer to solution.py in the current directory only. Do not write to /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/problems-3090/05_topk_bitonic or to the source repository's problems/ tree.

"""Naive top-k reference: torch.topk over the last dim.

This is the correctness oracle. The agent's solution must produce the same
top-k values (and equivalent indices modulo ties) within the tolerance
declared in problem.yaml. Note that solution.py is FORBIDDEN from calling
torch.topk / torch.sort / torch.kthvalue (see problem.yaml).
"""
import torch
import torch.nn as nn

OP_TYPE = "topk"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Top-k over the last dim of a 2D tensor.

    Input:
        x: (batch, n) fp32
    Output:
        values:  (batch, k) fp32, sorted descending
        indices: (batch, k) int64, into the last dim of x
    """

    def __init__(self, batch: int, n: int, k: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.batch, self.n, self.k = batch, n, k
        # No learned parameters, but declare a dummy buffer so state_dict
        # is non-empty and load_state_dict(strict=True) is meaningful.
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1))

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        values, indices = torch.topk(x, k=self.k, dim=-1, largest=True, sorted=True)
        return values, indices


# Module-level shims rebuilt by check.py / benchmark.py per shape.
batch = 64
n = 8192
k = 8

    # fp32 input drawn from a roughly Gaussian distribution; ties unlikel

"""Correctness runner for TopK.

Runs solution.Model vs reference.Model across all shapes in shapes.py, 3 seeds
each. Top-k correctness has two parts:

  1. VALUES: sol_values must match ref_values within fp32 tol. Both are
     returned sorted descending, so positional comparison is well-defined.
  2. INDICES: lenient — we do NOT require sol_indices == ref_indices because
     ties in x can yield multiple valid index sets. Instead we gather x at
     sol_indices and check those values match ref_values within tol. This
     catches "wrong indices" without false-failing on legitimate tie-breaks.

"""Canonical shape sweep for TopK.

Mix of:
  - decoder vocab top-k (single sequence, very large n, moderate k) — pure
    bandwidth test; the input read dominates everything.
  - prefill / batched attention top-k (many rows, moderate n, small k) — tests
    per-row parallelism and shared-memory bitonic networks.
  - non-power-of-2 n stress case — bitonic sort networks naturally want
    powers of two; this forces the agent to handle padding or partial sorts.
  - small-k limit — k=1 (argmax) is a degenerate but useful sanity case.
"""

"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.

All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.

Methodology:
  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.

Notes / known biases not addressed here:
  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
    "compiled" baseline policy.
  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
    instrumentation if you ever care.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

under a few scale regimes that catch kernels that only work for the nominal
N(0, 1)-ish inputs.

"""Top-k for RTX 3090 (SM86), shape-adaptive.

The reference uses a multi-pass radix select (~8 passes for fp32). These shapes
are tiny (each row is 16 KB - 512 KB), so per-call time is dominated by kernel
work, not DRAM. Two kernels cover the deck, picked per (k, n):

  * Small k (1, 8, 16) -- per-row register cascade. One block per row; each
    thread streams a strided slice keeping a sorted-descending register buffer
    of size K (the K largest it has seen). Buffers are merged across the block
    by a log2(BLOCK)-deep merge-tree in shared mem (stride K+1 to dodge 32-way
    bank conflicts). All-register, static-index cascade (a dynamic index into a
    register array spills to local memory; a shared-mem min-heap was tried and
    is slower due to shmem load latency in the dependent sift-down).

  * Large k (32, 64) -- per-row radix-256 histogram select. Four byte-passes
    (MSB first) build the monotonic uint of the k-th largest via a 256-bin
    histogram, then gather + in-shmem bitonic sort. ~12 barriers total vs ~96
    for a 1-bit radix, and 4x fewer row reads -- far cheaper than the O(n*K)
    cascade once K is large.

  * The single very-large row (n=131072, k=64) -- segmented radix: many blocks
    each radix-select their contiguous segment to top-K into a temp buffer,
    then one block radix-selects the merged candidates. Keeps the whole GPU
    busy instea

"""Custom top-k kernel for RTX 3090 (SM86).

Returns the k largest values per row of a (batch, n) fp32 tensor, sorted
descending, with their int64 indices -- same contract as the reference, but
implemented from scratch in CUDA (no library selection/sort calls).

Design
------
The deck is bandwidth/launch bound: each row read is tiny (0.5-2 MB), so the
wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel-launch + dispatch overhead, not by the
selection compute. Two levers:

  1. A lean single custom kernel (block-per-row) that reads each element once
     and keeps a per-thread local top-k, then a shared-memory merge-tree
     reduces the block to its top-k.  For the single very-large row
     (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot saturate DRAM, so the row is split
     across BPR blocks (each emits a partial top-k) and a second tiny kernel
     merges the BPR partials.

  2. Reusable output buffers (allocated once per Model) plus optional CUDA-graph
     capture/replay, which collapses per-call launch + Python dispatch overhead
     to a single graph launch -- the dominant cost on these shapes.
"""

import torch.nn as nn

#include <cfloat>

#define MAXK

__global__ void kernel_pass1(
    const float* __restrict__ in_val,
    float* __restrict__ out_val,
    int64_t* __restrict__ out_idx,
    int batch, int n, int k, int blocks_per_row, int chunk_size
) {
    int row = blockIdx.y;
    int chunk = blockIdx.x;

    int end_idx = start_idx + chunk_size;
    if (end_idx > n) end_idx = n;
    
    float thread_vals[64];
    int64_t thread_idxs[64];
    for (int i=0; i<k; ++i) {
        thread_vals[i] = -1e38f;
        thread_idxs[i] = -1;
    }
    
    int offset = row * n;
    for (int i = start_idx + threadIdx.x; i < end_idx; i += blockDim.x) {
        float v = in_val[offset + i];
        if (v > thread_vals[k - 1]) {
            int pos = k - 1;
            while (pos > 0 && v > thread_vals[pos - 1]) {
                thread_vals[pos] = thread_vals[pos - 1];
                thread_idxs[pos] = thread_idxs[pos - 1];
                pos--;
            }
            thread_vals[pos] = v;
            thread_idxs[pos] = i;
        }
    }
    
    __shared__ float smem_v[64 * 64];
    __shared__ int64_t smem_i[64 * 64];

"""Single-pass top-k for RTX 3090 (SM86).

Block-per-row kernel: each thread streams a strided slice of its row,
maintaining a sorted-descending register buffer of size K. A shared-memory
merge-tree combines per-thread buffers into the block top-K (sorted desc).

For very large rows (n > 32768) a segmented two-launch path uses multiple
blocks per row to keep enough warps in flight for DRAM bandwidth.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import ctypes
import os
import subprocess

import torch
import torch.nn as nn

OP_TYPE = "topk"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]

_SEG_THRESHOLD = 1 << 15  # 32768

#include <cuda_runtime.h>

template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void insert_topk(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int gi) {
    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
    float carry = v;
    int carry_i = gi;
    bool active = false;
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
        if (carry > tv[i]) active = true;
        if (active) {
            float tf = tv[i];
            tv[i] = carry;
            carry = tf;
            int t2 = ti[i];
            ti[i] = carry_i;
            carry_i = t2;
        }
    }
}

template <int BLOCK, int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void merge_tree(float* sv, int* si, int nbuf) {
    constexpr int S = K + 1;
    for (int d = 1; d < nbuf; d <<= 1) {
        for (int base = threadIdx.x *

+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import ctypes
+import os
+import subprocess
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+
+OP_TYPE = "topk"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["fp32"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]
+
+_SEG_THRESHOLD = 1 << 15
+
+_CUDA_SRC = r"""
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+
+template <int K>
+__device__ __forceinline__ void insert_topk(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int gi) {
+    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
+    float carry = v;
+    int carry_i = gi;
+    bool active = false;
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
+        if (carry > tv[i]) active = true;
+        if (active) {
+            float tf = tv[i];
+            tv[i] = carry;
+            carry = tf;
+            int t2 = ti[i];
+            ti[i] = carry_i;
+            carry_i = t2;
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+template <int BLOCK, int K>
+__device__ __forceinline__ void merge_tree(float* sv, int* si, int nbuf) {
+    constexpr int S = K + 1;
+    for (int d = 1; d < nbuf; d <<= 1) {
+        for (int base = threadIdx.x * (2 * d); base + d < nbuf;
+             base += BLOCK * (2 * d)) {
+            float* A = sv + base * S;
+            int* Ai = si + base * S;
+            float* B = sv + (base + d) * S;
+            int* Bi = si + (base + d) * S;
+            float tmp[K];
+            int ti2[K];
+            int ia = 0;
+            int ib = 0;
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int c = 0; c < K; c++) {
+                float va = A[ia];
+                float vb = B[ib];
+                if (va >= vb) {
+                    tmp[c] = va;
+                    ti2[c] = Ai[ia];
+                    ia++;
+                } else {
+                    tmp[c] = vb;
+                    ti2[c] = Bi[ib];
+                    ib++;
+                }
+            }
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int c = 0; c < K; c++) {
+                A[c] = tmp[c];
+                Ai[c] = ti2[c];
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+    }
+}
+
+template <int K, int BLOCK>
+__global__ void topk_reduce_kernel(
+    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+    long long* __restrict__ out_idx, float* __restrict__ tmp_vals,
+    long long* __restrict__ tmp_idx, int batch, int n, int nseg, int seg_size)
+{
+    const int row = blockIdx.x;
+    const int seg = blockIdx.y;
+    if (row >= batch) return;
+    const int seg_start = seg * seg_size;
+    const int seg_end = (seg_start + seg_size < n) ? (seg_start + seg_size) : n;
+    const float* xrow = x + (size_t)row * n;
+
+    constexpr int M = BLOCK * (K + 1);
+    extern __shared__ float smem[];
+    float* sv = smem;
+    int* si = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sv + M);
+
+    float tv[K];
+    int ti[K];
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
+        tv[i] = -INFINITY;
+        ti[i] = 0;
+    }
+
+    constexpr int UTILE = 8;
+    const int len = seg_end - seg_start;
+    const int stride = BLOCK * UTILE;
+    int full = (len / stride) * stride;
+    for (int base = 0; base < full; base += stride) {
+        float vb[UTILE];
+        int ib[UTILE];
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int j = 0; j < UTILE; j++) {
+            int q = base + threadIdx.x + j * BLOCK;
+            vb[j] = __ldg(&xrow[seg_start + q]);
+            ib[j] = seg_start + q;
+        }
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int j = 0; j < UTILE; j++) {
+            insert_topk<K>(tv, ti, vb[j], ib[j]);
+        }
+    }
+    for (int q = full + threadIdx.x; q < len; q += BLOCK) {
+        insert_topk<K>(tv, ti, xrow[seg_start + q], seg_start + q);
+    }
+
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
+        int off = threadIdx.x * (K + 1) + i;
+        sv[off] = tv[i];
+        si[off] = ti[i];
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+
+    merge_tree<BLOCK, K>(sv, si, BLOCK);
+
+    if (nseg == 1) {
+        for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
+            out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = sv[i];
+            out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)si[i];
+        }
+    } else {
+        size_t slot = ((size_t)row * nseg + seg) * K;
+        for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
+            tmp_vals[slot + i] = sv[i];
+            tmp_idx[slot + i] = (long long)si[i];
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+template <int K, int BLOCK>
+__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
+    const float* __restrict__ tmp_vals, const long long* __restrict__ tmp_idx,
+    float* __restrict__ out_vals, long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int nseg)
+{
+    const int row = blockIdx.x;
+    const size_t base = (size_t)row * nseg * K;
+
+    constexpr int S = K + 1;
+    constexpr int M = BLOCK * S;
+    extern __shared__ float smem[];
+    float* sv = smem;
+    int* si = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sv + M);
+
+    int nbuf = nseg;
+    int np = 1;
+    while (np < nbuf) np <<= 1;
+    nbuf = np;
+    for (int b = threadIdx.x; b < nbuf; b += BLOCK) {
+        int dst = b * S;
+        if (b < nseg) {
+            int src = b * K;
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
+                sv[dst + i] = tmp_vals[base + src + i];
+                si[dst + i] = (int)tmp_idx[base + src + i];
+            }
+        } else {
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
+                sv[dst + i] = -INFINITY;
+                si[dst + i] = 0;
+            }
+        }
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+
+    merge_tree<BLOCK, K>(sv, si, nbuf);
+
+    for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < K; i += BLOCK) {
+        out_vals[(size_t)row * K + i] = sv[i];
+        out_idx[(size_t)row * K + i] = (long long)si[i];
+    }
+}
+
+template <int BLOCK>
+__global__ void argmax_kernel(
+    const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ out_vals,
+    long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int batch, int n)
+{
+    const int row = blockIdx.x;
+    if (row >= batch) return;
+    const float* xr = x + (size_t)row * n;
+    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    const int lane = tid & 31

The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.  The input is a 2D fp32 tensor and you return the top-k values and their int64 indices along the last dim, sorted descending, same contract as torch.topk(largest=True, sorted=True). Correctness tolerance is 1e-4 abs/rel on the values; index ties are handled leniently — what matters is the returned values match the reference to tolerance, not that the index sets are bitwise identical. The shapes you have to handle are batch=1 n=131072 k=64 (decoder vocab top-k over a Llama-size vocabulary), batch=64 n=8192 k=8 (prefill / attention top-k), batch=32 n=16384 k=32 (mid-size batched), batch=16 n=12000 k=16 (non-power-of-two n, which bitonic n

         super().__init__()

+    def _ensure_buffers(self, x: torch.Tensor):
+        if self._buf_device == x.device:
+            return
+
+        b, n, k = self.batch, self.n, self.k
+        self._out_vals = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)

You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.  The input is a 2D fp32 tensor and you return the top-k values and their int64 indices along the last dim, sorted descending, same contract as torch.topk(largest=True, sorted=True).     25	#include <cuda_runtime.h>

    27	template <int K>
    28	__device__ __forceinline__ void insert_topk(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int gi) {
    29	    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
    30	    float carry = v;
    31	    int carry_i = gi;
    32	    bool active = false;
    33	    #pragma unroll
    34	    for (int i = 0; i < K; i++) {
    35	        if (carry > tv[i]) active = true;
    36	        if (active) {
    37	            float tf = tv[i];
    38	            tv[i] = carry;
    39	            carry = tf;
    40	            int t2 = ti[i];
    41	            ti[i] = carry_i;
    42	            carry_i = t2;
    43	        }
    44	    }
    45	}

You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py. Correctness tolerance is 1e-4 abs/rel on the values; index ties are handled leniently — what matters is the returned values match the reference to tolerance, not that the index sets are bitwise identical. import torch
import solution
m = solution.Model(128, 4096, 1).cuda().eval()
x = torch.randn(128, 4096, device='cuda')
with torch.no_grad():
    m(x)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
try:
    with torch.cuda.graph(g):
        y = m(x)
    g.replay()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    print('GRAPH_OK', y[0].shape, y[1].shape)
except Exception as e:
    print('GRAPH_FAIL', type(e).__name__, str(e))

You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py. Correctness tolerance is 1e-4 abs/rel on the values; index ties are handled leniently — what matters is the returned values match the reference to tolerance, not that the index sets are bitwise identical. import torch
import solution
m = solution.Model(128, 4096, 1).cuda().eval()
x = torch.randn(128, 4096, device='cuda')
with torch.no_grad():
    m(x)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
try:
    with torch.cuda.graph(g):
        y = m(x)
    g.replay()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    print('GRAPH_OK', y[0].shape, y[1].shape)
except Exception as e:
    print('GRAPH_FAIL', type(e).__name__, str(e))

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        if not x.is_contiguous():
            x = x.contiguous()
        self._ensure_buffers(x)
        out_vals = self._out_vals
        out_idx = self._out_idx

        if x.is_cuda and not self._graph_failed:
            key = int(x.data_ptr())
            graph = self._graphs.get(key)
            if graph is not None:
                graph.replay()
            else:
                try:
                    self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
                    torch.cuda.synchronize()
                    graph = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
                    with torch.cuda.graph(graph):
                        self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
                    graph.replay()
                    self._graphs[key] = graph
                except Exception:
                    self._graph_failed = True
                    self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)
        else:
            self._launch(x, out_vals, out_idx)

        return out_vals, out_idx

    x = torch.randn(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32)

    return [batch, n, k]
